< Date>
1596190422071<//Date>
<rating>5</rating>< Review>
Wanted to check out San Leandro's Farmer Market and what it had to offer.  This is a wonderful farmer's market in downtown San Leandro.  It is opened on Wednesdays from 4-8pm.  There is an abundant amount of merchants who are selling organic produce, fruits, eggs, flowers, desserts and ready made food.  I gotta make a shout for Alonso's Food!  He was really nice, patient and answered all my questions with a smile on his face.  He sells breads, assorted pastries, ready made pizzas, empanadas and cookies.  You want it, he got it. I can vouch that his products are top notch!  Too bad he doesn't have a retail store, but he also sells at Bayfair's Farmer Market on Saturday from 9am-1pm.  There is a small parking lot and ample street parking.  Just be aware that some have meters while others a couple of steps away do not.</Review>

<user_id>102127821011132310638< /user_id><name>Ankit Patel< /name><date>1598792091413< /date><rate>5</rate>< Review>
The San Leandro Farmers‚Äô Market is a popular family recreation activity that‚Äôs open seasonally from spring through fall.

It features the best locally and regionally grown produce, as well as other items like fresh flowers and baked goods, prepared food items, and arts and crafts.

The market is held downtown on Parrott Street. It frequently offers additional entertainment, including live music, wine and food tastings, cooking classes, and fun kid‚Äôs activities like art classes and face painting booths.

The season varies slightly from year to year, so check online or ask a local before heading out.</Review>

< text>
This place is awsome. I never thought I would go to a gas station just to order food. It's all made to order, fresh and hot. It's a great value light lunch; most sandwiches also come with a side. There breakfast sandwiches are good too. They got a great ham and cheese you just have to know to order it.</text>

< Text>
The price is decent and the restaurant is located in front of a badminton gym. I like that it's out of the way but the food is only decent. It hits the spot but not sure if they could survive in a much more competitive neighborhood.</Text>
<pics>None<//pics><response>None< /response>< GmapID>
0x80c2db6a08889749:0x8d6728cef6e78a6c</GmapID>
</record></dataset><record>
<gmap_id>0x80c2db6a08889749:0x8d6728cef6e78a6c< /gmap_id><Review>Little disclaimer before we start: I'm Indonesian, came in a group of 5 (all Indos), 2 have roots from Kalimantan/Borneo, one of which is from Singkawang and the other from Pontianak (not far from Singkawang). I must emphasize, This Is The Bomb.

Main dishes we got:
- Bakmi Singkawang: literally my favorite bowl of noodles in the entire LA county, like seriously. The texture and the flavor is just so on point, it puts other Indonesian noodle shops to shame (*cough* West Covina). To be fair, it doesn't have the same taste as your average noodles because it does have a slight vinegar taste, but that complements the flavors this dish has to offer. Like usually I'm the type of person to drown my noods in soup (don't @ me) but this? Heck no, the flavors are just too perfect that it shines, even without the soup 10/10
- Kwetiau Goreng Singkawang: solid dish, the kwetiau has a mild wok flavor, and the toppings are just seasoned perfectly to complement those noodles. I'm personally not a kwetiau girl, would probably have chosen the mie goreng instead but it's okay because this is still fire.
- Sup Sayur Asin: we didn't order this soup but it came with two of our dishes mentioned above (I think). But, I kid you not, this is the best sayur asin I've had in a long long time, probably better than most I've had in Indo. It has a bit of pork pieces in the bottom and the veggies in it aren't smelly at all (it's common for the veggie to be smelly). Honestly I would come back just for this soup ngl
- Nasi Campur: it came with the thick clear gravy sauce (not sure what it's called) but if it doesn't, just ask for it. I loved this one but I think it's missing something, maybe the broth isn't salty enough? Maybe the rice wasn't soft enough? I'm not even sure. For those wondering: the pork belly was super fat (which I love) but I know not everyone is super into that.
- Nasi Capcai: super nostalgic because it tastes exactly like what I used to eat; the veggies are still a bit crunchy which I know some people prefer. Definitely one of the healthier options or if you want to eat more veggies.

Appetizers & Others:
- Hakong: 8/10 without the sauce, 10/10 with the sauce. Bruh. That sauce is magic I swear. It complements the hakong so well with some balanced sweetness, sourness, and savoriness. Without it, it needs just a touch more salt but I think it's meant to be eaten with the sauce, so I'm not complaining haha.
- Choi pan: according to my friends, these are not singkawang style, but it's super delicious nonetheless. The sauce is the one that came with our kwetiau but it's delicious and spicy, but not as watery as the one I'm used too. The filling itself is super flavorful (with quite a good amount of white pepper), the wrapper is kinda chewy/bouncy in a good way--and is not too thick.
- Es doger: omfg they have ketan singkong and kolang kaling in it!! They had some interesting stuffs in it like popping boba and lychee jelly I think but I don't really mind it lol. The drink part is not overwhelmingly sweet, just the right amount for this dessert (I'm sure they use Marjan syrup)
- Sambal terasi: if yall need more spicy, do ask for this. You're welcome.

General situation:
Came when LA had outdoor dining open, but not indoor (3/13). I heard they're going to have both indoor and outdoor next week. Their outdoor seating is a spacious patio with some heater to keep you warm. The owners and workers are all Indonesian, with the owners originally from Singkawang. I know they serve Thai food but we didn't really ask why nor try it. All of the utensils and plates were single use (paper plates to serve the food, styrofoam plates for us to share), except for the bowls used for the noodles and soups where they used legit noodle bowls.

TL;DR: they have awesome Indonesian food that everyone must try. If you think Borneo Kalimantan Cuisine is good, try this one and you'll be blown away. 10/10 would come back and bring my Indo and non-Indo friends and families here!!</Review>< username>
Helen Limanto<//username>

<Rating>3<//Rating>< Review>
One of the few Indo-Thai restaurant in the area; honestly it's more of a resto vibe than a cafe. We came over dinner and ordered the mini-lumpia (10pcs) rolls and Pad Thai veggie. Food was tasteful and flavorful. However, during the course of our meal we saw a tiny black hair strand on the the pad Thai. Hence, we didn't finish the food. I'm sure its an isolated case but deeply disappointed nevertheless. On the positive side, their service was moderately fast. Prices are fair. Menu is somewhat limited from main Entree (e.g., No Nasi Rendang) to Appetizer. Staff were attentive, amiable and professional. Ample of parking spot. Overall, I will give it a try again and hopefully they will rectify the unsanitary issue.<//Review>

<user_name>Mark Teng</user_name>< Text>
If you are thinking about ordering takeout from Singkawang Cafe (they offer delivery via Uber Eats), my suggestion is to avoid this option. Actually, considering their rudeness and disregard for customer service, my suggestion would be to find an alternative location. Singkawang Cafe messed up an order of 6 items from Uber Eats, preparing only half the items ordered (total of 3/6 prepared). That's okay, people make mistakes. When I called, they said that they messed up the order, and apologized, they could clearly see the order chit which had six items on it. I was upset at this point because my wife and children were hungry and we had half of our order ready. But the icing on the cake was when we spoke to the restaurant management in person, they changed their story saying that it was Uber Eats that made the mistake, only sending half the order to them. It is this dishonesty that made me write this review. Mistakes made, yes, it happens. Lying about it to the customer to cover your mistakes, that's another story. All we asked for was for the restaurant to cover the delivery charge since we had to go pick up the order ourselves (we even told them restaurant credit would be fine), and we were refused. I've ordered from this restaurant several times previously, but this time would be our last. Very disappointing.<//Text>

I take my dogs here every time I leave town and they do a good job looking after them. My dogs are excited to go there which I see as a good sign and clearly like the staff. The prices are good and I've never had a problem. I take my dogs about once per month on average. I recommend to friends.

< Review>
Do yourself a favor, reserve a storage unit HERE!

Not only does it include amazing customer service by friendly, professional staff but it's also an affordable price for LA in a navigable location. Don't forget the convenience of managing your account online while having a flexible month to month contract :)

Obviously everyone knows that moving is stressful. My move was especially stressful, not because the fact I was moving from San Diego, but everything that you think could and couldn't go wrong...went wrong. From broken boxes from accident prone movers and sitting in traffic with empty gas tanks to wrong keys by missing landlords and ruined newly bought furniture and mishandled sentimental belongings- I begged the day to be over and naturally I dreaded my last stop:storage. Seriously I'm considering to believe in angels because when I went there, I easily spotted and found parking right away. I was greeted sincerely and helped right away!
